commission or governing authority on plat of subdivision required for filing or recording in superior court clerks office ocga  15667d article i  in general purpose and intent of chapter it is with the intent of creating a climate conducive to the orderly and progressive growth of the city a climate of mutual and reasonable understanding with prompt and just consideration to the various interests involved in subdivisional work that the procedures and requirements set forth in this chapter have been established similarly community interests require the regulation and control of development to ensure reasonable protection of property values and to promote a healthy environment for the citizens of the city the regulations contained in this chapter have been formulated and adopted for the purpose of promoting the health safety and morals and the general welfare of the people of the city    definitions the following words terms and phrases when used in this chapter shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning block means a piece or parcel of land entirely surrounded by public highways or streets other than alleys in cases where the platting is incomplete or disconnected the subdivider may determine the outline of the block crosswalk means a rightofway within a block dedicated to public use ten feet or more in width intended primarily for pedestrians and from which motorpropelled vehicles are excluded and which is designed to improve or provide access to adjacent roads or lots lot means a portion of a subdivision intended as a unit for transfer of ownership or for development or both in determining the area and dimensions of a lot no part of the rightofway of a road or crosswalk may be included lot width means the width of the lot at the building line measured parallel to the street rightofway line master plan means a comprehensive plan which may consist of several maps data and other descriptive matter for the physical development of the city or any portion thereof including any amendments extensions or additions thereto recommended by the planning commission indicating the general location for major roads parks or other public open spaces public building sites routes for public utilities zoning districts or other similar information planning commission means the planning commission of the city setback line or building line means the minimum horizontal distance between the street rightofway line or the street centerline where appropriate and the building or any projection thereof except 1 steps terraces and open fire escapes  2 balconies canopies or cornices projecting not more than three feet beyond the main building wall  or 3 offset or overlapping portions of the second floor of the building that do not extend more than three feet beyond the main wall of the building streets and alleys means ways for vehicular traffic whether designated as a street highway thoroughfare parkway throughway road avenue boulevard lane place or however otherwise designated 1 alleys means minor ways which are used primarily for vehicular service access to the back or the side of properties otherwise abutting on a street 2 collector streets means those which carry traffic from minor or neighborhood streets to the major system of streets and highways including the principal entrance streets of a residential development and streets for circulation within such a development 3 major streets and highways means those which are used primarily for fast or heavy traffic 4 marginal access streets means minor streets which are parallel to and adjacent to major streets and highways and which provide access to abutting properties and protection from 5 minor streets means those which are used primarily for access to the abutting properties subdivider means any person corporation or duly authorized agent who undertakes the subdivision of land subdivision 1 the term subdivision means the division development or redivision of a lot tract or parcel of land regardless of how it is to be used into two or more lots either by plat or by metes and bounds description or the division or redivision of land involving the dedication of a new park playground street or other public rightofway or facility  or the vacation realignment or any other change in existing streets alleys easements recreational areas water areas or other public improvements or facilities and when appropriate to the context shall relate to the act or process of subdividing or to the land subdivided 2 for the purposes of this chapter the following are excepted from the term subdivision a any subdivision of land for agricultural purposes provided no lot thereby produced has an area of less than ten acres and an average width of from 400 feet and where no new streets roads or other rightsofway are involved b the sale or exchange of parcels of land between owners of adjoining properties provided that additional lots are not thereby created and that the lots created are not reduced below the minimum sizes required by this chapter or the zoning regulations of the city c the transfer of unsubdivided land or a lot or parcel of land established by deed or plat recorded among the land records of the city prior to the effective date of the regulations from which this chapter was derived d the division or sale of land by judicial decree    variances a conditions the planning commission shall have authority to vary and modify the provisions of this chapter  provided however that in granting variances and modifications the planning commission may require such conditions as will in its judgment secure substantially the objectives of the standards or requirements so varied or modified b hardship where the planning commission finds that extraordinary hardship may result from strict compliance with the regulations established in this chapter it may vary the regulations so that substantial justice may be done and the public interest secured  provided however that such variation will not have the effect of nullifying the intent and purpose of the master plan or this chapter c largescale development the standards and requirements of the regulations established in this chapter may be modified in the case of a plan and program for a complete community or a neighborhood unit which in the judgment of the planning commission provides adequate public spaces and improvements for the circulation recreation light air and service needs of the tract when fully developed and populated and which also provides such covenants or other legal provisions as will ensure conformity to and achievement of the plan information may include data on existing covenants land characteristics and available community facilities and utilities and information describing the subdivision proposal such as number of residential lots typical lot width and depth price range minimum floor area in structures business areas playgrounds park areas and other public areas proposed protective covenants and proposed utilities and street improvements c letter of application a written letter of application as specified in section 4426d may be used by the subdivider to comply with the requirements enumerated in this section    preliminary plats and data for conditional approval a preliminary plat seven copies of blueline prints shall be required the preliminary plat shall be drawn at a scale of not less than 100 which the proposed subdivision is to be recorded with names of owners and certification of a registered professional civil engineer or registered land surveyor 7 scale datum north arrow date of survey date of plat and land lot and district numbers c draft of protective covenants one copy of the draft of protective covenants whereby the subdivider proposes to regulate land use in the subdivision and otherwise protect the proposed development shall be required d written application two copies of the written application containing essentially the same descriptive information specified in section 4425b shall be submitted with the preliminary plat the application may be used to fulfill the requirements of section 4425b and if completed properly and accurately under section 4425b need not be resubmitted    proposed subdivision names and proposed street names not to duplicate other subdivisions and streets the proposed names of the subdivision and proposed street names shall not duplicate or too closely approximate phonetically the name of any other subdivision or street in the city    plats and data for final approval a scale  data required four blueline prints of the final plat shall consultation with building official prior to the preparation of the subdivision plat the subdivider shall confer with the building official who shall review the sketch plan of the proposed subdivision to determine whether the subdivision meets the requirements of this chapter this step does not require formal application or filing of the plat with the planning commission b favorable consideration by building official upon receiving favorable consideration of the building official the subdivider may then proceed to prepare the preliminary plat for submission to the planning commission c favorable consideration by building official not to constitute approval favorable consideration by the building official under no circumstances shall be construed as preliminary or tentative approval of the subdivision    conditional approval of preliminary plat a preparation on reaching conclusions informally as described in section 4460 regarding his general program and objectives the subdivider shall cause to be prepared a preliminary plat together with other supplementary material as deemed necessary by the building official and specified in section 4428 b submission to planning commission four copies of the preliminary plat and supplementary material specified together with two copies of a written letter of application for conditional approval of the preliminary plat shall be submitted to the planning commission at least seven days prior to the meeting at which it is to be considered c conditional approval or disapproval within 30 days after the submission of the preliminary plat and other material submitted for consideration the planning commission shall express its approval as conditional approval and state the conditions of such approval if any or if disapproval shall express its disapproval and its reasons therefor d noting of action of planning commission the action of the planning commission shall be noted on two copies of the preliminary plat referenced and attached to any conditions determined one copy shall be returned to the subdivider and the other retained by the planning commission e conditional approval not to constitute final approval conditional approval of a preliminary plat shall not constitute approval of the final plat rather such conditional approval shall be deemed an expression of approval of the layout submitted on the preliminary plat as a guide to the preparation of the final plat which will be submitted for approval of the planning commission upon fulfillment of the requirements of this chapter and the conditions of the conditional approval if any    shortform procedure for conditional approval of preliminary plat a subdivision having five lots or less with lots fronting a previously dedicated street and abutting all adjacent properties which have been previously subdivided and if the platting of the subdivision does not affect any major alterations of utility installation may be subdivided under the shortform subdivision procedure prescribed as follows 1 preapplication the preapplication procedure as described in section 4460 shall be performed 2 design standard and data the design standard and data of the filing plat of the shortform subdivision shall be identical when applicable to those of the longform subdivision plats 3 preparation of preliminary plat on reaching conclusions informally as described in section 4460 regarding his general program and objectives the subdivider shall cause to be prepared a preliminary plat together with other supplementary material as deemed necessary by the building official and specified in section 4428 4 submission of preliminary plat to building official four copies of the preliminary plat and supplementary material specified together with two copies of a written letter of application for conditional approval shall be submitted to the building official 5 conditional approval conditional approval shall be given to the subdivider by the building official within five days after the submission of the written letter of application preliminary plat and supplementary material when the proposed subdivision meets the design standards of the subdivision regulations established in this chapter the action of the building official shall be noted on two copies of the preliminary plat referenced and attached to any conditions determined one copy shall be returned to the subdivider and the other retained by the building official 6 preparation of final plat after obtaining conditional approval from the building official the subdivider may then proceed to prepare the final plat 7 omission of preliminary submission procedure the preliminary submission procedure as prescribed in section 4426 shall be omitted in the shortform subdivision procedure    approval of final plat a preparation the final plat shall be prepared as specified in section 4428 and shall conform substantially to the preliminary plat as approved and if desired by the subdivider it may constitute only that portion of the approved preliminary plat which he proposes to record and develop at the time  provided however that such portion conforms to all requirements of the regulations established in this chapter b submission of performance bonds all performance bonds must be submitted to the city prior to approval of final plat by the planning commission c submission of final plat to planning commission the final plat and other supplementary material required for approval shall be submitted to the planning commission at least seven days prior to the meeting at which it is to be considered it shall also be required that such material shall be submitted to the planning commission within six months after approval of the preliminary plat  otherwise such approval shall become null and void unless an extension of time is applied for and granted by the planning commission d action by planning commission within 30 days after the submission of the final plat and supplementary material required for approval the planning commission shall express its final action e recording upon approval  costs all final plats upon approval shall be recorded with the county clerks office the subdivider shall bear all costs of recording    secs 44644484  reserved article iii  design standards division 1  generally suitability of land for development purposes the planning commission shall not approve the subdivision if from adequate investigation conducted by any public agency concerned it has been determined that in the best interest of the public the site is not suitable for development purposes of the kind proposed    land subject to flooding or deemed topographically unsuitable land subject to flooding and land deemed to be topographically unsuitable shall not be platted for residential occupancy nor for such other uses as may increase danger to health life or property or aggravate erosion or flood hazard such land within the plot shall be set aside for such uses as shall not be endangered by periodic or occasional inundation or shall not produce unsatisfactory living conditions    preservation of trees when feasible all trees of major growth shall be preserved any oak tree having a diameter greater than 14 inches shall be preserved in the development of a subdivision when necessary to accomplish use of the land the mayor and council may allow a variance from this rule upon petition    secs 448844117  reserved division 2  blocks factors considered in determination of length width and shape the lengths widths and shapes of blocks shall be determined with due regard to 1 provision of adequate building sites suitable to the special needs of the type of use contemplated  2 zoning requirements as to lot sizes and dimensions  3 needs for convenient access circulation control and safety of street traffic  and 4 limitations and opportunities of topography    desirable maximum length the desirable maximum block length is 1200 feet    desirable minimum length the desirable minimum block length is 500 feet    secs 4412144138  reserved division 3  lots general size dimension and setback of lots the lot size width depth shape and orientation and the minimum building setback lines shall be appropriate for the location of the subdivision and for the type of development and use contemplated    dimension requirements lot dimensions shall conform to the requirements of the zoning regulations if such requirements are more stringent otherwise minimum lot dimensions shall be as follows minimum lot dimensions minimum frontage 75 feet minimum depth 150 feet minimum area 11250 square feet building setback from centerline of street 75 feet    width of corner lots for residential use corner lots for residential use shall have an extra width when the normal width is less than 75 feet to permit appropriate building setback from and orientation to both streets    front upon public street each lot shall front upon a public street    double frontage and reverse frontage lots to be avoided  planting screen double frontage and reverse frontage lots shall be avoided except where essential to provide separation of residential development from traffic arteries or to overcome specific disadvantages of topography and orientation a planting screen reservation of at least ten feet and across which there shall be no right of access shall be provided along the line of lots abutting such a traffic artery or other disadvantageous use    requirements for side lot lines side lot lines shall be substantially at right angles or radial to street lines    secs 4414544171  reserved division 4  streets conformity to master plan a the arrangement character extent width grade and location of all streets shall conform to the master plan and shall be considered in their relation to existing and planned streets to topographical conditions to public convenience and safety and in their appropriate relation to the proposed uses of the land to be served by such streets b where such is not shown in the master plan the arrangement of streets in a subdivision shall either 1 provide for the continuation or appropriate projection of existing principal streets in surrounding areas  or 2 conform to a plan for the neighborhood approved or adopted by the planning commission to meet a particular situation where topographical or other conditions make continuance or conformance to existing streets impracticable    minor streets to be laid out so as to discourage minor streets shall be so laid out that their use by will be discouraged    subdivision abutting on proposed major street  marginal access streets planting and other treatments where a subdivision abuts or contains an existing or proposed major street the planning commission may require marginal access streets reverse frontage with screen planting contained in a nonaccess reservation along the rear property line deep lots with rear service alleys or such other treatment as may be necessary for adequate protection of residential properties and to afford separation of local traffic    requirements where subdivision borders on railroads and limited access highway rightsofway where a subdivision borders on or contains a railroad rightofway or limited access highway rightofway the planning commission may require a street approximately parallel to and on each side of such rightofway at a distance suitable for the appropriate use of the intervening land as for park purposes in residential districts or for commercial or industrial purposes in appropriate districts such distances shall also be determined with due regard for the requirements of approach grades and future grade separations    reserve strips reserve strips controlling access to streets shall be prohibited except where their control is definitely placed in the city    street jogs street jogs with centerline offsets of less than 125 feet shall be avoided    intersections to be at right angles street intersections shall be as nearly at right angles as practicable    radius at intersections at each street intersection the property line at each block corner shall be rounded with a curve of radius r varying with the interior angle as specified in the following table unless sufficient data is presented to show that strict adherence to this requirement is impractical due to topographical or engineering considerations table of intersection returns interior angle in degrees intersection of two minor streets r in feet any intersection on major streets r in feet 150145 12 15 145140 12 18 140135 12 20 13585 12 25 8575 20 40 7565 30 70 6555 40 80 5545 50 100 450 75 140    rightofway widths street rightofway widths shall be as shown in the master plan and where not shown therein shall be no less than as follows minimum rightofway widths street type rightofway in feet minimum major 80 collectorcommercial and residential 70 minor 60    half streets half streets shall be prohibited except where essential to the reasonable development of the subdivision and where it is determined to be practicable to require the dedication of the other half when the adjoining property is subdivided the other half of the street shall be platted within such tract    platting of deadend streets deadend streets may be platted where the planning commission deems desirable and where the land adjoins property not subdivided in which case the streets shall be carried to the boundaries of the land    permanent deadend streets  length and turnaround requirements deadend streets designed to be so permanently shall not be longer than 600 feet and shall be provided at the closed end with a turnaround having an outside roadway diameter of at least 80 feet and a street rightofway diameter of at least 100 feet    street names no street names shall be used which will duplicate or be confused with the names of existing streets street names shall be subject to the approval of the planning commission    street grades a street grades wherever feasible shall not exceed the following with due allowance for reasonable vertical curves maximum street grades street type percent grade major 7 collector 10 minor 12 b no street grade shall be less than one percent    secs 4418644208  reserved division 5  easements provided where subdivision traversed by watercourse drainageway natural channel or stream where a subdivision is traversed by a watercourse drainageway natural channel or stream there shall be provided an easement conforming substantially to the limits of such watercourse plus additional width as necessary to accommodate future construction as recommended by the building official    utility easements to be avoided where possible utility easements shall be avoided except in unusual cases where no other satisfactory arrangements can be provided for the installation of utilities    permission required for dedication of utility easements permission must be obtained from the building official for the dedication of utility easements prior to the submission of such dedication    pedestrian easements pedestrian easements not less than ten feet wide may be required where deemed essential to provide circulation or access to schools playgrounds shopping centers transportation and other community facilities    secs 4421344232  reserved division 6  public sites and open spaces required  percentage of gross area  factors considered by planning commission proposed subdivisions shall provide appropriate open spaces suitably located and of reasonable size for parks playgrounds play lots playfields or other recreational areas as may be necessary such area should consist of approximately five percent of the gross area of the proposed subdivision in determining this requirement the planning commission shall give due consideration to the adequacy of existing parks and recreational facilities in the vicinity size and characteristics of the subdivision and whether or not such requirement will result in exceptional hardship to the subdivider    dedication to city  reservation for public use under private ownership parks and playgrounds may be dedicated to the city or reserved for public use under private ownership if so dedicated the land shall be used exclusively by the city for recreational purposes and the subdivider may stipulate a reasonable limit of time within which the city is required to make physical improvements to the site otherwise the title of the site will revert to the subdivider    size and location subject to approval the size and location of parks and playgrounds shall be subject to the approval of the planning commission    combining of areas where subdivision too small to provide suitable open space where the proposed subdivision is too small to provide space of suitable size for the public open space use intended the open space provided may be combined with that provided or to be provided in an adjoining area thus in the aggregate there will be provided an open space of suitable size for the purpose intended    sites for public schools where a site for a public school building is deemed suitable by the planning commission and the proper school authority in a subdivision such site shall be reserved for public usage the subdivider shall allow a period of 45 days from the date of submittal of the preliminary plat during which time the proper school authority is required to make known the intention of acquiring the site if such notification is affirmative the planning commission shall then set the period of time upon consulting the subdivider and the school authority for such acquisition    secs 4423844267  reserved article iv  required improvements posting of performance bond the subdivider is required to file with the city a performance bond which is available to the city and in sufficient amount to ensure completion of all street and sewer improvements or in lieu of such bond the subdivider may submit performance bonds by contractors for street improvements and sewer construction of the proposed subdivision to ensure such completion of all street and sewer improvements    approval of plans  inspection of work the building official must approve plans for and inspect and approve construction of all subdivision work the county health department must approve plans for the use of sewerage septic tanks or other sanitary facilities    posting of surety bond for maintenance of pavement and drainage system the subdivider is responsible for maintenance of pavement and the drainage system in the subdivision for a period of one year and is required to post with the city a surety bond in the amount of ten percent of the performance bond required pursuant to section 44268 to ensure the completion of streets and roads such bond shall be valid for a period of one year beginning on the date of final acceptance of the streets by the city    effect of failure of subdivider to correct defect upon notification if upon being notified of the failure of the pavement or drainage system the subdivider does not correct the deficiency or commence work within ten days of the notice such failure shall be deemed to be a failure on the bond and the city shall have the right to make the necessary repairs either by public work or by private contract and the bond shall be liable for the full amount of the cost of the repairs    underground work to be completed prior to laying of pavement all underground work consisting of sewers water lines gas mains and telephone conduits shall be installed and the earth backfill compacted before pavement is laid    approval of plans and profiles for street improvements two copies of the complete plans and profiles for street improvements shall be submitted for approval of the building official prior to approval of the final plat by the planning commission    required street improvements street improvements shall be provided in each subdivision as prescribed in the following 1 grading grading shall be done by the developer streets shall be graded to a width of not less than 42 feet in the center of the rightofway to provide for a 26foot pavement and two eightfoot shoulders 2 curbing granite or concrete curb shall be furnished by the developer any curb damaged after being set and before pavement is completed shall be reset by the developer 3 paving pavement shall be furnished and paid for by the developer pavement shall consist of four inches of stone penetrated with two gallons of ac 8 asphalt choked with 35 pounds of choke stone no 89 and topped with 100 pounds of hot plant asphalt per square yard 4 sidewalks in heavily congested areas developers will be required to lay a concrete sidewalk of a minimum width of four feet four inches in thickness and a 28day compressive strength of 2500 psi 5 driveways driveways from the edge of the pavement to the property line shall be constructed of concrete of sixinch minimum thickness and a 28day compressive strength of 3000 psi 6 markers street markers similar to the citys markers shall be furnished and set at all street intersections by the developer    sanitary sewers a required sewers shall be laid in all streets service connections installed to property lines and connections made to trunk line sewers or a master septic tank b septic tanks individual septic tanks will be permitted only by special permission of the county health department c costs the developer shall bear all costs of sanitary facilities d approval of plans and profiles two copies of the complete plans and profiles for sanitary sewers shall be submitted for approval of the building official prior to approval of the final plat by the planning commission    storm drainage adequate storm drain pipes and catchbasins shall be installed by developers    water mains water mains shall be laid in all streets and service connections installed to property lines by developers    monuments iron pins of no less than 24 inches long nor less than onehalf inch in diameter shall be set flush with the ground at every lot iii  lodging excise tax footnotes  3  state law reference municipalities authorized to levy and collect tax on the furnishing for value to the public of rooms lodgings or accommodations ocga  481351 definitions the following words terms and phrases when used in this article shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning due date means the 20th day after the close of the monthly period for which the tax is to be computed estimated tax liability means the lodging providers prospective tax liability based upon the average monthly tax remittance in the prior fiscal year as adjusted for change in tax rate or substantial change in circumstances due to damage to the hotel folio means primary documentation produced by a hotel that demonstrates interaction between the lodging provider and the occupant and which at a minimum reflects the name and address given by the occupant the dates of occupancy the amount of rent charged for each date together with the amounts of applicable excise tax and the methods of payment guest room means accommodations occupied or intended arranged or designed for transient occupancy by one or more occupants for the purpose of living quarters or residential use hotel means any facility or any portion of a facility including any lodginghouse roominghouse dormitory turkish bath bachelor hotel studio hotel motel motor hotel auto or trailer court truckstop tourist cabin campground lodge inn timeshare or other condominium apartment community public club or private club containing guest rooms and which is occupied or is intended or designed for occupancy by paying guests whether rent is paid in money goods labor or otherwise the term hotel does not include any hospital asylum sanitarium orphanage jail prison or other facility in which human beings are housed and detained under legal restraint lodging provider means any person operating a hotel in the city including but not limited to the owner or proprietor of such premises lessee sublessee lender in possession licensee or any other person operating such hotel  and who is subject to the taxation imposed for furnishing for value to the public any rooms lodgings or accommodations monthly period means the calendar months of any year occupancy means the use or possession or the right to the use or possession of any guest room in a hotel or the right to the use or possession of the furnishings or to the services and accommodations accompanying the use and possession of the guest room occupant means any person who for a consideration uses possesses or has the right to use or possess any guest room in a hotel under any lease concession permit right of access license to use or other agreement or otherwise permanent resident means any occupant who as of a given date has or shall have occupied or has or shall have the right of occupancy of any guest room in a hotel for not less than 30 continuous days next preceding such date rent means the consideration received for occupancy valued in money whether received in money or otherwise including all receipts cash credits and property or services of any kind or nature and also the amount for which credit is allowed by the lodging provider to the occupant without any deduction therefrom whatsoever tax means the tax on occupants imposed by this article as provided for by ocga  481350 et seq specifically ocga  481351  132011 tax rate there shall be paid for every occupancy of a guest room in a hotel in the city a tax at the rate of five percent of the amount of rent unless an exemption is provided under section 4663  132011 collection of tax by lodging provider every lodging provider furnishing guest rooms in a hotel in the city shall collect a tax of five percent on the amount of rent from the occupant unless an exception is provided under section 4663 the lodging provider shall provide a receipt to each occupant which receipt shall reflect both the amount of rent and the amounts of this and other tax applicable this tax shall be due from the occupant and shall be collected by the lodging provider at the same time that the rent is collected the lodging provider shall be liable to the city for the full amount received or collected as tax whether collected appropriately or inappropriately  and for any amount of tax that should have been collected but was not 1 any person who receives or collects the tax or any consideration represented to be the tax from another person holds the amount so collected in trust for the benefit of the city and is liable to the city for the full amount collected plus penalty and interest 2 an individual who controls or supervises the collection of the tax from another person or an individual who controls the accounting for or remittance of the tax and who willfully fails to remit or cause to be remitted the tax is liable as a responsible individual for an amount equal to the tax not remitted or caused to be remitted plus penalty and interest the dissolution of a corporation partnership or other business or fraternal association does not affect a responsible individuals liability under this subsection furthermore the liability imposed by this subsection shall be in addition to any other penalty provided by law  132011 exceptions no tax shall be collected from an occupant after becoming a permanent resident  or from an occupant who certifies in writing that he is staying in such accommodations as a result of his residence having been destroyed by fire or other casualty  or from the united states and the state or any instrumentality of either thereof  or from any official or employee of the state its units of local government or any other instrumentality of the state when traveling on official business and presenting written substantiation thereof or paying by state or local government credit or debit card  or from a foreign sovereign enjoying exemption by treaty or consular convention when presenting substantiation issued by the united states department of state occupancy provided without charge in money or otherwise is not subject to this tax  132011 registration of lodging provider  form and contents  execution  certificate of authority every person engaging or about to engage in business as a lodging provider in the city shall immediately register with the city clerk on a form provided by said official persons engaged in such business must so register not later than 30 days after the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived such registration shall set forth the name under which such person transacts business or intends to transact business the location of his place of business and such other information which would facilitate the administration of the tax as prescribed by the city clerk the registration shall be signed by the owner if a natural person  in case of ownership by an association or partnership by a member or partner  in case of ownership by a corporation by an officer the city clerk shall after such registration issue without charge a certificate of authority to each lodging provider to collect the tax from the occupant a separate registration shall be required for each place of business of a lodging provider each certificate shall state the name and location of the business to which it is applicable  132011 determination generally  returns  payments a due date of taxes all amounts of such tax shall be due and payable to the city clerk monthly on or before the 20th day of the month next succeeding the respective monthly period the tax shall become delinquent for any monthly period after the 20th day of each succeeding month during which it remains unpaid b penalty and interest for failure to pay tax by due date a lodging provider who fails to make any return or to pay the amount of tax as prescribed shall be assessed a specific penalty to be added to the tax in the amount of five percent or $500 whichever is greater if the failure is for one month or less  and an additional five percent or $500 whichever is greater for each additional month or fraction thereof in which such failure shall continue  provided however that the aggregate penalty for any single violation shall not exceed 25 percent or $2500 whichever is greater delinquent amounts shall bear interest at the rate of one percent per month or fraction thereof until paid c acceptance of delinquent return and remittance without imposing penalty and interest  authority  requirements if the failure to make any return or to pay the amount of tax by the due date results from providential cause shown to the satisfaction of the governing authority of the city by affidavit attached to the return and remittance is made within ten days of the due date such return may be accepted exclusive of penalty and interest d waiving of penalty and interest  authority ocga  48241 relating to the authority to waive interest and ocga  48243 relating to the authority to waive penalty shall apply  provided however that the governing authority shall stand in lieu of the state commissioner of revenue and the city shall stand in lieu of the state e penalty for fraud in the case of a false or fraudulent return or of failure to file a return where willful intent exists to defraud the city of any tax due a penalty of 50 percent shall be assessed f return  remittance  time of filing  lodging providers required to file  contents on or before the 20th day of the month succeeding each monthly period a return for the preceding monthly period together with appropriate remittance shall be filed with the city clerk the return shall report the gross rent taxable rent exempt rent amount of tax collected or otherwise due for the period and such other information as may be required by the city clerk however if the estimated tax liability for any monthly period shall exceed $250000 for a lodging provider who in the prior fiscal year remitted tax greater than $250000 in any three consecutive months such lodging provider shall file an estimated return and remit not less than 50 percent of the estimated tax liability for the monthly period by the 20th day of that same monthly period the amount of tax so remitted shall be credited against the amount to be due with the regular return for the monthly period to be filed on the 20th day of the succeeding month g extension of time of filing  authority  requirements  remittance  penalty and interest the mayor and council of the city may for good cause extend the time for making returns for not longer than 30 days no extension shall be valid unless granted in writing upon written application of the lodging provider such grant may not be applicable for longer period than 12 consecutive months a lodging provider granted an extension shall remit tax equaling not less than 100 percent of the tax paid for the corresponding period of the prior fiscal year  such remittance to be made on or before the date the tax would otherwise come due without the grant of extension no penalty or interest shall be charged during the first ten days of the extension period thereafter interest shall be collected on the unpaid balance at the rate of one percent per month h collection fee allowed lodging providers lodging providers collecting the tax shall be allowed a percentage of the tax due and accounted for and shall be reimbursed in the form of a deduction in submitting reporting and paying the amount due if the amount is not delinquent at the time of payment the rate of the deduction shall be three percent of the amount due but only if the amount due was not delinquent at the time of payment  132011 deficiency determinations a recomputation of tax  authority to make  basis of recomputation if the city clerk is not satisfied with the return of the tax or the amount of the tax period in respect to which the lodging provider failed to make the return and shall be based upon any information which is or may come into the possession of the city clerk written notice shall be given in the manner prescribed in section 4666c b penalty and interest for failure to pay tax penalty and interest shall be assessed upon the amount of any determination as provided by section 4665 to collect the amount delinquent together with penalty interest court fees filing fees attorneys fees and other legal fees incident thereto b lodging provider selling or quitting business if any lodging provider liable for any amount under this article sells out his business or quits his business he shall make a final return and remittance within 15 days after the date of selling or quitting the business c duty of successors or assignees of lodging provider to withhold tax from purchase money if any lodging provider liable for any amount of tax interest or penalty under this article sells he shall be personally liable for the payment of the amount required to be withheld by him to the extent of the purchase price e credit for tax penalty or interest paid more than once or erroneously or illegally collected whenever the amount of any tax penalty or interest has been paid more than once or has been erroneously or illegally collected or received by the city it may be refunded by the mayor and council if the lodging provider or person determines that he has overpaid or paid more than once which fact has not been determined by the city clerk such person shall have three years from the date of payment to file a claim in writing stating the specific ground upon which the claim is founded the claimant may request a hearing before the mayor and council at which the claim and any other information available will be considered the mayor and council shall approve or disapprove the claim and notify the claimant of its action  132011 administration of article  recordkeeping a may prescribe  132011 violations a any lodging provider who fails neglects or refuses to collect the tax as provided by section 4662 shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall be punished by a fine of not more than $50000 or confinement for a term not to exceed three months or both b any lodging provider who fails or refuses to make any return as provided by section 4665 to keep adequate records or to open them for inspection by the city or to furnish other data reasonably requested by the mayor and council shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall be punished by a fine of not more than $50000 or confinement for a term not to exceed three months or both c any lodging provider who makes a false or fraudulent return with intent to evade the tax shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall be punished by a fine of not less than $50000 nor more than $100000 or confinement for a term not to exceed three months or both d each and every day during any portion of which any violation is committed continued or permitted shall constitute a separate offense and shall be punished accordingly  132011 traffic and vehicles article i  in general uniform rules of the road adopted the provisions of ocga  4061 known as the uniform rules of the road are hereby adopted as and for the traffic regulations of this city with like effect as if recited in this section    temporary regulations authorized in cases where the traffic upon the streets of the city may become congested or upon occasions of parades or at theaters churches or schools or any public gathering or assemblage at any park building or public place the police may make temporary rules regulating the traffic any person who violates such regulations after having been warned of such temporary traffic regulations shall be guilty of a violation of this chapter    traffic speed truck parking and other zones  designation by signs and traffic control devices  schedule  specifications of devices  violations a designation and maintenance of traffic control signs markings and devices the chief of police or his designee upon approval by ordinance of the mayor and council is authorized to designate and maintain with appropriate traffic control signs markings and devices after engineering and traffic investigations 1 speed zones  2 truck routes and streets to be designated specifically to prohibit various classes of trucks  3 oneway streets and other directional control devices  4 freight loading zones and regulations  5 parking and no parking zones and regulations thereon  6 stop yield and other rightofway signs  and 7 stop signals and other traffic signals b issuance of orders designating certain areas the chief of police or his designee is authorized to issue written orders designating by appropriate traffic control signs markings and devices after engineering and traffic investigations 1 pedestrian crosswalks  2 other safety zones for pedestrians  3 traffic lanes  and 4 any other sign marking or zone necessary for orderly and safe conditions on the streets of the city c schedule the chief of police shall maintain or cause to be recorded a current schedule of all traffic rules regulations and orders under this chapter which record shall be available for inspection by the public for items listed in subsection a of this section this schedule and any amendments thereto shall become effective only upon approval thereof by ordinance of the mayor and council this schedule is hereby incorporated in this section and copies shall be available for public inspection in the office of the city clerk d specifications of devices all traffic control signs signals devices and markings shall conform to specifications in the manual on uniform traffic control devices adopted by the state transportation board all signs and signals required under this section for a particular purpose shall so far as practicable be uniform as to type and location throughout the city all traffic control devices so erected and not inconsistent with the provisions of state law or this section shall be official traffic control devices of the city e violations any violation of any traffic zone marking sign or other traffic control device established under this section shall be a violation of this chapter    authority to close streets and divert traffic the police shall have the authority in the interest of public safety or convenience to close any street alley or portion of the same temporarily to vehicular or foot traffic or divert such traffic therefrom    use of closed streets whenever any street alley or sidewalk or any portion thereof is closed by order of the mayor or police department or any other designated authority whether the closing is for repairs improvements protection against danger or for any other purpose it shall be unlawful for any person to enter cross or travel upon the portion so closed except by permission of the authorities closing the same    duty to secure load it shall be unlawful for the operator of a vehicle to haul trash refuse ashes dirt sand concrete mix gravel stone coal brick steel shavings or any other material in such a manner as to cause such material to be scattered over any street of the city    hitching to vehicles no person shall hitch or climb onto any moving vehicle either with or without the consent of its operator provided that this section shall not apply to the coupling of trailers or proper towing of other vehicles    speed of trains within city railroad trains traveling within the city shall not be operated at a speed in excess of 40 miles per hour at no time shall railroad trains be operated at a speed in excess of what is reasonably safe with due regard to attendant circumstances    secs 4894834  reserved article ii  vehicle operation free flow of traffic  obstruction all persons are prohibited from engaging in driving procedures or any other activities which obstruct the free flow of traffic in around over and streets alleyways and other public ways of the city any person is prohibited from stopping his vehicle except at a stop signal or stop sign or to honor another drivers rightofway or in an emergency situation in a manner as to obstruct the free and orderly flow of traffic by the maneuver or to engage in unduly slow driving procedures so as to obstruct the free flow of traffic or to needlessly circle and block or dawdle or make unnecessarily rapid accelerations and decelerations or to in any other manner constitute a traffic nuisance or hazard    speed limits established a no person shall operate any motor vehicle or tractor upon any of the streets and highways of the city at a greater speed than is reasonable and proper having regard to the width traffic and use of the streets and highways or so as to endanger the property or life or limb of any person b thirty miles per hour shall be the maximum speed on all streets or portions of streets within the city unless otherwise indicated by officially posted signs designating the maximum vehicular speed upon those streets as approved by the mayor and council    slowmoving heavily laden vehicles to keep to right slowmoving or heavily laden vehicles shall not be driven abreast upon any highway but one must follow behind the other and keep as near to the righthand curb as practicable    uturns it shall be unlawful to turn a vehicle on a street so as to proceed in the opposite direction commonly known as making a uturn at any intersection at which a traffic control signal is in place or at any other intersection or place where signs have been erected by the police department prohibiting such turns    secs 48394864  reserved article iii  stopping standing and parking vehicle to stop at curb  exceptions a vehicle shall not stop elsewhere than at the curb except in an emergency or to allow another vehicle or pedestrian to cross in front of it or pursuant to the directions of a traffic control signal or the signal of a traffic officer    parking in alleys vehicles shall not park in public alleys  provided however that vehicles may park in public alleys not longer than necessary to load and unload and when so parked such vehicles shall stand as close as possible to one side of such alley in order to permit other vehicles to traverse such alley    duty to remove disabled or stalled vehicle whenever a vehicle becomes stalled upon a street or when because of damage or other reason it cannot be moved by its own power and consequently blocks the street or interferes with the use of the street by other vehicles it shall be the duty of its owner or operator to remove the vehicle by towing or otherwise within a reasonable time    regulations at specific locations the mayor and council may from time to time regulate restrict or prohibit the standing or parking of vehicles on specified streets or parts of streets or in specified areas signs or markings shall be installed and maintained giving notice of such regulations restrictions and prohibitions and it shall be unlawful to violate or fail to comply with the directions of any such sign or marking    vehicles to be parked within marked spaces whenever a space is marked off on any street for the parking of an individual vehicle every vehicle there parked shall be parked within the lines bounding that space    manner of loading and unloading freight and merchandise when practicable merchandise and freight shall be discharged and loaded from the side of the vehicle nearest the curb when such handling is impracticable because of the size or weight of the merchandise or freight the vehicle may back to the curb but it shall not stand at any angle which will interfere with the operation of other vehicles    secs 48714898  reserved article iv  truck routes definitions the following words terms may also authorize other departments as may be deemed necessary to support enforcement  9039 secs 50325050  reserved article iii  sewer use division 1  generally definitions the following words terms and phrases when used in this article shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning biochemical oxygen demand bod means the calculated pounds of oxygen required to satisfy the fiveday oxygen demand of 1000000 pounds of waste when tested in accordance with the procedure given in the latest edition of standard methods published by the american public health association building sewer means that part of the horizontal piping of a building drainage system extending from the outside of the building or end of the inside plumbing system to and including the connection with the city sewer system city sewer system means such system composed of sanitary sewers storm sewers combined sewers and sewage treatment works owned by a city combined sewer means a sewer intended to receive domestic sewage treated or weak industrial wastes surface water and stormwater domestic sewage means liquid from residences business buildings or institutions which has a daily average of not more than 400 parts per million of bod and a like amount of suspended solids industrial wastes means the liquid wastes resulting from processes employed in industrial establishments an industrial waste will be considered weak when it contains less than 600 parts per million of bod and suspended solids with no biologically toxic substances in it ph means a measure of acidity or alkalinity which has a range of zero to 14 sanitary sewer means a sewer intended to receive domestic sewage and treated or weak industrial waste without the admixture of surface water stormwater or unpolluted industrial process water storm sewer means a sewer intended to receive stormwater and surface water street wash or drainage and sewage and industrial wastes that have been completely purified suspended solids means the amount of material in suspension expressed in parts per million as determined by the gooch crucible method given in the latest edition of standard methods published by the american public health association    notice of violation whenever it is found that any person is violating any of the provisions or requirements set out in this article a written notice stating the offense and setting a time limit for the correction shall be served upon the offender by the chief of police the offender shall within the time limit stated in the notice served upon him forever cease all violations a   unsanitary deposits it shall be unlawful for any owner or lessee to place deposit or permit to be deposited any human excrement garbage or any other organic waste upon the premises in an unsanitary manner    discharge of polluted waters to streams ditches or other underground water source it shall be unlawful to discharge any untreated domestic sewage industrial wastes or other polluted waters into any streams or ditches or any abandoned water well or in any way to discharge sewage or industrial waste directly into underground waters within the area controlled by the city    connection required where property within 200 feet of city sewer system it shall be unlawful to construct or maintain any privy privy vault cesspool or septic tank intended for or subject to receiving organic wastes wherever a connection can be made to the city sewer system within 200 feet of any property    connection to be at owners expense  time within which to connect the owner of all houses buildings or properties situated within the city abutting on any streets alleys or parkways in which there is now located or may hereafter be located any sewer pipeline of the sanitary sewer system of the city is hereby required at his own cost and expense to install suitable toilet facilities and to connect those houses or buildings erected upon the property directly with the sanitary sewer system within three months after notice to do so    connection of properties beyond city limits any person owning or controlling premises located beyond the corporate limits of the city and desiring to install a plumbing system on the premises and connect the system with the sanitary sewers of the city may do so by complying with the requirements of this article and by paying a monthly sewer rental charge    method of disposal where sewer unavailable or connection cannot be made where city sewers are not available or where a connection as determined by the mayor and council cannot be made a septic tank or another method of private sewage disposal must be constructed according to the requirements of the state department of natural resources    citys right of entry authority is hereby granted to the duly authorized city employees to enter upon all properties to make all necessary inspections tests and measurements to ensure complete compliance with all of the regulations of this article    secs 50605076  reserved division 2  building sewers separate sewers required  exception a separate building sewer is required for each individual building or house whether constructed as a detached unit or as one or a pair or row but a single building sewer will be permitted to serve an apartment house or other multiple unit structure or industrial plant whose individual apartments or units are not subject to separate ownership    connection to be at owners expense  permit to connect required building sewers from the point of entry of the city sewer to the building shall be laid by the owner at his expense but only after such connections have been authorized by a permit issued by the superintendent of utilities upon the submission of evidence by the owner that the discharge from the building sewer will comply with all of the regulations of this article    use of old building sewers and drains old building sewers and drains may be used in connection with new buildings or new plumbing only when they are approved of a permit as for new construction of building sewers    diameter and fall all building sewers shall be not less than six inches in diameter and shall have a fall of not less than onehalf inch per foot for sixinch pipe and not less than onequarter inch per foot for pipe eight inches or over in diameter    laying of pipes all pipe shall be laid on a uniform grade and where possible on a straight line where the building sewer cannot be laid on a straight line curved pipe shall be used for every deflection from a straight line of more than three inches per foot    recommendation where sewer near large tree trunks where building sewers are within 20 feet of large tree trunks it is recommended that cast iron pipe with leaded joints be used all joints must be filled made smooth and absolutely watertight    manner of connecting building sewer to city sewer the connection between the building sewer and the city sewer shall be made at the y branch provided if no y branch was left in the city sewer for the building sewer and the city sewer is not over 12 inches in diameter a y branch shall be installed in the city sewer at the desired location by the owner of the building sewer where the city sewer is over 12 inches in diameter and where no y branch was left for the building sewer a hole may be cut in the city sewer large enough to receive the end of the building sewer and the connection made so that the building sewer enters the city sewer at an angle of 45 degrees a 45degree ell can be used to make this connection if the spigot end is cut to fit so that it does not extend past the inside surface of the city sewer city sewers shall not be tapped below the centerline of the city sewer    backfilling in backfilling the material shall be carefully placed and packed around the pipe to provide a uniform bearing and to keep the pipe in proper position no stones bricks or like material shall be used in the backfill until there has been a depth of at least 18 inches of fine earth or gravel placed over the pipe    maintenance of barricades and lights proper barricades and lights must be maintained on the banks of the trenches to guard the public against accidents during construction or connection of the building sewer    secs 508650113  reserved division 3  discharge of deleterious wastes prohibited discharges to sanitary sewers no stormwater from pavements areaways roofs or other sources shall be admitted to the sanitary sewers which are designed to be used exclusively as carriers of domestic sewage and suitable industrial wastes the same shall apply to unpolluted process or cooling waters    discharge of stormwater stormwater shall be admitted only to such sewers as are specifically designed as combined sewers or storm sewers    discharge of liquids and gases above certain temperatures no person shall discharge into any sewer any liquid or gas having a temperature greater than 100 degrees fahrenheit    prohibited discharges to public sewers no person shall discharge or deposit any of the following described waste materials into any sanitary storm or combined sewer 1 liquid waste materials which contain more than 100 parts of oil or grease per million parts determined by weight  2 liquid waste material in which the suspended solids exceed 600 parts per million determined by weight  3 any petroleum product or other product which by reason of its nature or quality may cause a fire or explosion or in any way be injurious to persons or to the sewer system  4 any industrial waste with a ph of less than 55 or greater than 90  5 any industrial waste with a fiveday biochemical oxygen demand of more than 600 parts per million by weight  6 any industrial waste containing any toxic or poisonous substance in a sufficient quantity to interfere with the biologic processes used in the sewage treatment process or that will pass sewage treatment plant and harm persons or aquatic life in the receiving stream  7 any unshredded garbage scraps or vegetables  or 8 any straw ashes cinders shavings butchers offal rags feathers or any other material capable of causing obstructions nuisance or injury to or interference with the sewer system    sampling manholes a required in certain instances every building sewer discharging industrial wastes from any plant or establishment into the city sewer system may be required at the discretion of the approving authorities to have a sampling manhole for the purpose of ascertaining the quality and quantity of the waste flowing in the building sewer b location  construction the manhole shall be located at a suitable and satisfactory location and it shall be not less than three feet in inside diameter and built in a manner designated by the superintendent of utilities c cost the cost of the manhole shall be borne by the applicant but the manhole shall become the property of the city government d maintenance the responsibility for maintaining the manhole in a safe condition shall be assumed and remain with the owner of the property at all times    pretreatment of wastes whenever the industrial wastes do not meet the requirements of this article or the quantity of biochemical oxygen demand is onetenth of the total of the entire wastes of the city the industry will be required to pretreat its waste or enter into a oneyear agreement with the city to treat the waste as discharged    secs 5012050136  reserved article iv  underground 50142 no person may excavate in a street highway public space or a private easement of an operator or near the location of a utility installed on the premises of a customer served by such utility or demolish a building without having first ascertained in the manner prescribed in sections 50140 and 50141 the location of all underground utilities in the area that would be affected by the proposed excavation or demolition each operator shall maintain a list of all underground utilities and plants or maps showing their location    notice of intent a except as provided in section 50142 before commencing any excavation or demolition operation designated in section 50139 each person responsible for such excavation or demolition shall serve written or telephone notice of intent to excavate or demolish at least three but not more than ten full working days to the state utility protection center prior to any such excavation or demolition b the written or telephonic notice required by subsection a of this section must contain the name address and telephone number of the person filing the notice of intent and if different the person responsible for the excavation or demolition the starting date anticipated duration and type of excavation or demolition operation to be conducted the location of the proposed excavation or demolition and whether or not explosives are to be used c if notification required by this section is made by telephone an adequate record of such notification shall be maintained by the superintendent at the city hall    response to notice of intent each operator or designated representative notified in accordance with section 50140 shall not less than two working days in advance of the proposed excavation or demolition unless a shorter period is provided by agreement between the person responsible for the excavation or demolition and the operator or designated representative supply by use of maps when appropriate the following information to the person responsible for the excavation or demolition 1 the approximate location and description of all of its underground utilities which may be damaged as a result of the excavation or demolition  2 the location and description of all utility markers indicating the approximate location of the underground utilities  and 3 any other information that would assist that person in locating and thereby avoiding damage to the underground utilities including providing adequate temporary marking indicating the approximate location of the underground utility in locations where permanent utility markers do not exist    emergency compliance with the notice requirements of section 50140 is not required of persons responsible for emergency excavation or demolition to ameliorate an imminent danger to life health or property  provided however that such persons give as soon as practicable oral notice of the emergency excavation or demolition to each operator having underground utilities located in the area where such excavation or demolition is to be performed and requests emergency assistance from each operator so identified in locating and providing immediate protection to its underground utilities an imminent danger to life health or property exists whenever there is a substantial likelihood that loss of life health or property will result before the procedures under sections 50140 and 50141 can be fully complied with    damage a except as provided by subsection b of this section each person responsible for any excavation or demolition operation designated in section 50139 that results in any damage to an underground utility shall immediately upon discovery of such damage notify the operator of such utility of the location and nature of the damage and shall allow the operator reasonable time to accomplish necessary repairs before completing the excavation or demolition in the immediate area of such utility b each person responsible for any excavation or demolition operation designated in section 50139 that results in damage to an underground utility permitting the escape of any flammable toxic or corrosive gas or liquid shall immediately upon discovery of such damage notify the operator police and fire departments and take any other action as may be reasonably necessary to protect persons and property and to minimize the hazards until the arrival of the operators personnel or police and fire departments    precautions to avoid damage in addition to the notification requirements of section 50140 each person responsible for any excavation or demolition operation designated in section 50139 shall 1 plan the excavation or demolition to avoid damage to or minimize interference with underground utilities in and near the construction area  2 maintain a clearance between an underground utility and the cutting edge or point of any mechanized equipment taking into account the known limit of control of such cutting edge or point as may be reasonably necessary to avoid damage to such utility  and 3 provide such support for underground utilities in and near the construction area including during backfill operations as may be reasonably necessary for the protection of such utilities    secs 5014550171  reserved article v  catv franchise fee per consumer choice for television act the city shall collect a fee of five percent of the operators gross revenues as provided by law for any cable or video state franchise issued in the corporate boundaries by the state pursuant to ocga  36761 et seq known as the consumer choice for television act of 2007 res of 712008 vehicles for hire article i  in general secs 5215218  reserved article ii  taxicabs division 1  generally presumption of operation any automobile marked labeled or identified by lettering or numbers as a taxicab and found upon the streets of the city or regularly used for transportation of passengers shall be presumed to be used as a taxicab and for transportation of passengers for hire for the purpose of this article    identification and marking of vehicles a all motor vehicles operated as taxicabs in the city shall be marked on the outside with the following information 1 the name of the owner  2 the word taxicab or taxi  3 if a fleet or more than one taxicab is operated by one company or owner a number shall be assigned to each vehicle which shall be individual and identifying  and 4 any other information which may be deemed necessary by the mayor and council b the markings described in subsection a of this section shall be stenciled or painted on each side of the taxicab in a permanent paint of contrasting color to the color of the vehicle or affixed by decal or some like manner the letters of such markings shall not be less than three inches in height and must be printed so that the markings may be easily read at a distance of at least 50 feet    certificate of vehicle inspection required the owner and operator of each taxicab licensed to operate within the city shall before having his license either granted or renewed produce to the city manager a written inspection report from a qualified automobile mechanic engaged in business within the city such mechanic shall be approved by the mayor and council showing that the brakes and lights on each unit operated by him are in safe serviceable condition the license shall in no case be granted until this section is complied with    sale trade or exchange of vehicle a notice required if any owner or operator of a taxicab in the city shall sell trade or exchange any taxicab being operated in the city and substitute another car therefor it shall be the duty of the seller to notify the city clerk within ten hours of the sale trade or exchange of the vehicle giving the number under which the car traded is identified in the policy of liability insurance on file with the mayor and council b transfer of insurance required it shall also be the duty of such owner or operator of the car substituted to furnish the clerk written endorsement of the insurance company issuing the public liability policy the endorsement to be attached as an endorsement on the liability policy showing that the car substituted is insured under the terms of the liability insurance    driversminimum age no person shall drive a taxicab upon the streets of the city who is less than 19 years of age    driverseffect of felony conviction no person shall drive a taxicab upon the streets of the city who has been convicted of an offense constituting a felony or who has pleaded guilty upon a charge of having committed an offense constituting a felony    driversdriving under influence of intoxicating liquor it shall be unlawful for any person licensed to drive a taxicab under the provisions of this article to operate such taxicab while he is under the influence of intoxicating liquor a violation of this section shall be grounds for license revocation    transporting alcoholic beverages a prohibited it shall be unlawful for any person operating a licensed taxicab service in the city or any driver operating a taxicab in the city under the license to knowingly haul wine liquor or beer in such taxicab provided that this section shall not apply to a driver transporting a farepaying passenger in possession of alcoholic beverages so long as such alcoholic beverages remain in the possession and control of the passenger and are not opened within the vehicle b revocation of license if the driver of any taxicab in the city knowingly allows or permits intoxicating liquor wine or beer to be hauled in the taxicab operated by him in violation of this section the license issued by the city shall automatically be revoked if any license is forfeited and revoked because a driver is guilty of hauling intoxicating liquor wine or beer and desires to be heard he shall have a right to appeal to the mayor and council for a hearing and be heard at such time and place as the mayor and council shall designate pending the hearing before the mayor and council the licensee shall not operate the taxicab service under and by virtue of any such license c forfeiture of drivers rights it shall be unlawful for any driver guilty of knowingly hauling liquor wine or beer in any taxicab driven by him to again drive a taxicab in the city    number of passengers no person shall drive a taxicab upon the streets of the city when such vehicle contains more persons than such vehicle is designed to carry    receiving and discharging passengers drivers of taxicabs shall not receive or discharge passengers in the roadway but shall drive to the sidewalk or curb on the righthand side of such roadway and there receive or discharge passengers    secs 52295259  reserved division 2  occupational license required for drivers it shall be unlawful to drive a taxicab or vehicle of any kind for the purpose of transporting passengers or property for hire without first applying for and obtaining an occupational license therefor    required to engage in taxicab business it shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the business of furnishing taxicab service in the city and maintaining a place of business in the city without first obtaining a license approved by the mayor and council    application  manner and form application for a taxicab drivers license shall be made in such manner and form as prescribed by the city manager    statement to accompany application application for a license to drive a taxicab shall be supported by a sworn statement of the applicant setting forth the following 1 name and address of the applicant  2 the applicants age  3 the applicants habits as to sobriety  and 4 whether or not the applicant has been convicted of any offense against the laws of the state or of any city and particularly whether or not he has been convicted of violating any traffic regulation of any state or city    approval of application no license shall be issued to drive a taxicab until the application has been approved by the city manager    personal appearance of applicant the applicant shall submit himself personally before the city manager if required or if he so desires at the time the application for a taxicab drivers license is considered    action on application  issuance and denial  fees if upon a consideration of an application for a license to drive a taxicab the city manager shall decide that the applicant is qualified and entitled to operate a taxicab and in all manners in full compliance with all local state and federal laws having due regard to the safety and morals of the public the application shall be granted and a license issued by the city clerk upon payment of the business or occupation tax legally demandable if the city manager shall determine that the applicant is not a fit and proper person to be so licensed having due regard for the safety and morals of the public the mayor and council shall refuse such license    suspension or revocation authorized for good cause a the city manager shall have authority to suspend or revoke any and all licenses issued under this article for good cause shown or in the event the licensee fails to maintain compliance with any local state or federal law relevant to the operation of the licensed business after five days notice given the licensee at either a regular or special meeting it shall be unlawful for any licensee to operate during the period of suspension b the term good cause shall mean any violation of this of any state statutes pertaining to the operation of motor vehicles    revocation for failure to provide service it is the declared policy of the mayor and council that in licensing the operation of vehicles under this article a reasonable service will be rendered to the general public and to the inhabitants of the city by the persons holding those licenses and if such service cannot or will not be rendered by any person holding such license the license should be revoked among the causes justifying such revocation shall be unreasonable failure or refusal to render such service    secs 52695294
